<name>Cindy Wong<//name>< text>
The employees there were very friendly & accommodating.  The guys were pretty fast & efficient.  Rented 1 week at $130+ tax & called in to extend it for another 4 more days, $26+tax daily.  Ended up extending it for another 3 days so ended up renting the car for 2 weeks.  Instead of charging me daily for the 2nd week, they charged me the weekly rate at $130 +tax.  2 weeks = $260+tax.  Much less than at $26+ tax per day for the 2nd week which would've been $182 + tax for the 2nd week.  Saved about $50.  They also had time to give me a ride home when I dropped off my car.   The only negative was my rental had some dry stains on the seats.  Luckily,  it didn't smell so I assume they were water stains left from the previous renters.
I like the fact that the Toyota corolla had bluetooth & backup camera which are almost must haves.< /text>

< review>
Great hike! A bit more secluded so if you want a quieter hike this is the place to go to. It's a beginner hike with elevation gain mostly in the first mile. The one thing we forgot was bug spray which I regretted the next morning. (lots of mosquito bites).

We also took our dog on this hike since it was dog friendly.

The other issue is getting to this trail requires you to drive on some rough gravel road for at least 2 miles. Any car can make it, but it won't feel pleasant compared to an suv. We also saw a prius parked at the lot before the trail head as well.< /review>

< review>
Parker Lake (about 4.5 miles round trip)
Starting at the Parker Lake trailhead outside the small town of June, make your way up a slow incline in the sun. Look behind you (or just wait until your hike out) and see Mono Lake in the distance. The trail will peter out and leave you in the shaded company of a creek. After about two miles on the trail, you‚Äôll make it to the lake. Look across to see the waterfalls. Early summer will bring wildflowers; mid-fall, yellowing aspens.

Though it is possible to make your way around the lake, a little bushwhacking will be necessary. If peace is what you‚Äôre seeking, don‚Äôt venture all the way around but instead make your way to a log for a rest or bring your fly rod and try for the occasional trout.< /review>
